    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer17634613302644302061">The latest novel from the #1 internationally best-selling author of <i>The Alchemist.</i><br/><br/><i>There is nothing wrong with anxiety.<br/>Although we cannot control God's time, it is part of the human condition to want to receive the thing we are waiting for as quickly as possible.<br/>Or to drive away whatever is causing our fear....<br/>Anxiety was born in the very same moment as mankind. And since w</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17634613302644302061" style="display:none">The latest novel from the #1 internationally best-selling author of <i>The Alchemist.</i><br /><br /><i>There is nothing wrong with anxiety.<br />Although we cannot control God's time, it is part of the human condition to want to receive the thing we are waiting for as quickly as possible.<br />Or to drive away whatever is causing our fear....<br />Anxiety was born in the very same moment as mankind. And since we will never be able to master it, we will have to learn to live with it-just as we have learned to live with storms.</i><br /><br />* * *<br /><br />July 14, 1099. Jerusalem awaits the invasion of the crusaders who have surrounded the city's gates. There, inside the ancient city's walls, men and women of every age and every faith have gathered to hear the wise words of a mysterious man known only as the Copt. He has summoned the townspeople to address their fears with truth:<br /><br />"Tomorrow, harmony will become discord. Joy will be replaced by grief. Peace will give way to war.... None of us can know what tomorrow will hold, because each day has its good and its bad moments. So, when you ask your questions, forget about the troops outside and the fear inside. Our task is not to leave a record of what happened on this date for those who will inherit the Earth; history will take care of that. Therefore, we will speak about our daily lives, about the difficulties we have had to face."<br /><br />The people begin with questions about defeat, struggle, and the nature of their enemies; they contemplate the will to change and the virtues of loyalty and solitude; and they ultimately turn to questions of beauty, love, wisdom, sex, elegance, and what the future holds. "What is success?" poses the Copt. "It is being able to go to bed each night with your soul at peace."<br /><br />* * *<br /><br />Now, these many centuries later, the wise man's answers are a record of the human values that have endured throughout time. And, in Paulo Coelho's hands, The Manuscript Found in Accra reveals that who we are, what we fear, and what we hope for the future come from the knowledge and belief that can be found within us, and not from the adversity that surrounds us.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17634613302644302061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

  <span id="freeText2723649703402346113" style="display:none">When I first picked up the book, I compared it to Khalil Gibran's "The Profit". I was a bit disillusioned, and stopped reading for a bit. The 3 chapters I read that day were directly addressing issues I was experiencing at the time!<br /><br />This book is definitely one you want to read slowly, ponder on the messages and hopefully apply to your life. Its a book you want to keep in your personal library and refer back to it.<br /><br /><br />Paolo Coelho did not disillusion. </span>

<div id="review_982755388" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/982755388" />

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9786001181405" href="/book/show/22609882">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer982755388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17343691077252367893">Manuscrito encontrado em Accra, 2013 = Manuscript found in Accra : a novel, Paulo Coelho<br/>Manuscript Found in Accra is a novel by Brazilian author Paulo Coelho. The action is placed in 1099 in Jerusalem while the city awaits the invasion of the crusaders. Inside the city’s walls, men and women gathered to hear the wise words of a mysterious Greek man– known as the Copt. The people begin with questions about their fears, true enemies, defeat and struggle; they contemplate the will to change, and th</span>
  <span id="freeText17343691077252367893" style="display:none">Manuscrito encontrado em Accra, 2013 = Manuscript found in Accra : a novel, Paulo Coelho<br />Manuscript Found in Accra is a novel by Brazilian author Paulo Coelho. The action is placed in 1099 in Jerusalem while the city awaits the invasion of the crusaders. Inside the city’s walls, men and women gathered to hear the wise words of a mysterious Greek man– known as the Copt. The people begin with questions about their fears, true enemies, defeat and struggle; they contemplate the will to change, and the virtues of loyalty and solitude; and ultimately turn to questions of beauty, and elegance, love.<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز چهاردهم ماه ژوئن سال 2014 میلادی<br />عنوان: دستنوشته‌ ی آکرا؛ اثر: پائولو کوئیلو؛ م‏‫ترجم: ایلیا حریری‬، تهران، نشر نی، ‫1392، در 180 ص، شابک: 9789641853480‬‬؛ ‏موضوع: داستان‌های نویسندگان برزیلی -- سده 20 م<br />عنوان: دستنوشته‌ های آکرا؛ اثر: پائولو کوئیلو؛ ‏‫ترجمه: دل آرا قهرمان‬، مشخصات نشر: تهران، ذهن آویز، چاپ دوم ‫1393، در 180 ص، شابک: ‫‮‭9786001181405‬؛<br />داستان در جهان خیال و واقعیت می‌گذرد، نگارگر به روایت حکیمی یونانی، مشهور به کوپتا می‌پردازد، که در دست نوشته‌ هایی که سده ها بعد مردی انگلیسی آنها را کشف می‌کند، حضور دارد ...؛ اثری ویژه، با جملات جادویی و شگفت‌انگیز اثر پائولو کوئیلو است. در کتاب دستنوشته‌ های آکرا تشخیص بین واقعیت و داستان، آسان نیست، و هیچ مرزی برای هیچکدام، به چشم نمی‌آید. اساس این دست نوشته‌ ها ارزش‌ها هستند، که هرگز نمی‌توان آن‌ها را داستان دانست. این ارزش‌ها در طول زمان وجود خواهند داشت و جاری خواهند بود. در ماه دسامبر سال 1945 میلادی، دو برادر که در جستجوى مکانى براى استراحت بودند، در منطقه ی حمرا دام، در مصر علیا، در غارى پناه جستند، و در آنجا صندوقى پر از پاپیروس یافتند. به جاى اطلاع‌ دادن به مقامات محلى، آن دو تصمیم گرفتند آن‌ها را یکى یکى در بازار عتیقه بفروشند، تا توجه مقامات دولتى جلب نشود. مادر این جوانان که از «انرژى منفى» آن‌ها مى‌ترسید، تعدادى از پاپیروس‌هاى تازه کشف شده را سوزاند. سال بعد به دلایلى که تاریخ از آن‌ آگاه نیست، آن دو برادر با هم دعوا کردند. مادرشان که این نزاع را، نتیجه ی همان «انرژى‌هاى منفى» مى‌دانست، پاپیروس‌ها را به یک کشیش سپرد، و کشیش یکى از آن‌ها را به «موزه ی قبطى قاهره» فروخت. در آن‌جا عنوان: «نسخه خطى ناگ حمدى» را به پاپیروس‌ها دادند، که این نام هنوز روى آن‌ها هست (ناگ حَمَدى نزدیک‌ترین شهر مصر، به مکانی است که این نسخه‌ ها در آن پیدا شدند). یکى از کارشناسان موزه، تاریخ‌نویس ادیان، «ژان دورس» به اهمیت این کشف پى‌برد، و براى نخستین‌بار در سال 1948 میلادی، در مقاله‌ اى به آن اشاره کرد. سایر پاپیروس‌ها، کم‌کم در بازار عرضه شدند. این پاپیروس‌ها ترجمه یونانى متونى هستند، که بین اواخر سده نخست پیش از میلاد مسیح، تا سال 180 پس از میلاد مسیح، نوشته شده‌ اند و این مجموعه را «اناجیل اپوکریفال» نیز مى‌نامند، زیرا در اناجیل چهارگانه‌ اى که امروز مى‌شناسیم جایگاهی ندارند. نقل جملات برگزیده کتاب دست نوشته‌های آکرا: - باید به عشق اجازه نزدیک شدن بدهى. - ناکام کسى است که شکست را نمى‌پذیرد. - اگر شما هرگز تنها نباشید، نمى‌توانید خود را بشناسید. - هدف بزرگ ما در زندگى عشق است. باقى سکوت است. - تلاش نکنید که به هر قیمتى دوستتان بدارند، زیرا که عشق قیمت ندارد. - عشق تنها یک کلمه است تا زمانى که کسى از راه برسد و معنایى به آن بدهد. - «مشکلات» نام ابزارى قدیمى است که اختراع شده بود تا به ما کمک کند که خود را بشناسیم. - زخم‌ها مدال‌هایى هستند که در تن تو داغ آن‌ها به جا مانده است، و دشمن تو از آن‌ها خواهد ترسید. پایان نقل ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="17343691077252367893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17055869258999898965">Since I first read The Alchemist, I've always loved Paulo Coelho's books. I think this book is a MUST READ for every single soul on earth no matter which your religion or believes you've got.   <span id="freeText17055869258999898965" style="display:none">Since I first read The Alchemist, I've always loved Paulo Coelho's books. I think this book is a MUST READ for every single soul on earth no matter which your religion or believes you've got. It contains all the wisdom that should be taught in schools, instead of losing hours with stupid subjects about religion or ethics, it contains the essence of life. <br /><br />The author is humboldt enough to recognise that this is not his writing, which makes him even greater than what I thought.<br />It is just a transcription of a manuscript found in Jerusalem, the authentic one, and there is not a single word spoiled in it.<br />It is a book to keep for the rest of your life in a safe place and go to when needed.<br /><br />Simply brilliant.</span>

<div id="review_559284842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/559284842" />
    <a title="Kathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2336179-kathy"><img alt="Kathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375042944p2/2336179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/559284842?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy" href="/user/show/2336179-kathy">Kathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2336179-kathy?shelf=spirituality">spirituality</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559284842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3345848076570708125">This was a Goodreads First Reader Win, thanks.<br/><br/><br/>I would have adored this book when I was 17 or even 20. But alas, I am much, much, much older than that now and less fond than I was then of books full of quotable Words Of Wisdom.<br/>The premise of the book is poignant...the people are gathered before a time of great struggle and potential endings (and yeah, sure, it could well be a parable of our times, why not). They are of many faiths...Jewish, Christian, and Muslim, there in the lovely city of Jerus</span>
  <span id="freeText3345848076570708125" style="display:none">This was a Goodreads First Reader Win, thanks.<br /><br /><br />I would have adored this book when I was 17 or even 20. But alas, I am much, much, much older than that now and less fond than I was then of books full of quotable Words Of Wisdom.<br />The premise of the book is poignant...the people are gathered before a time of great struggle and potential endings (and yeah, sure, it could well be a parable of our times, why not). They are of many faiths...Jewish, Christian, and Muslim, there in the lovely city of Jerusalem where in 1099 everyone is living in peacefulness and delight, apparently. But the crusaders are about to attack. (wait, don't I recall that the crusaders were Christians?? But that's okay, History is not one of the book's themes). (actually, come to think of it, the set up is like the Gita too)<br />Anyway, as of course any bunch of people facing destruction or battle would do, they all sit around and listen to the mysterious dude who shows up to tell them diverting stories (in 1099 you couldn't just go on FB and alert your buddies that something was up). He's known only as The Copt.<br />In a style kind of like that of Gibran (when I was 17 I carried The Prophet with me everywhere, told you I would have liked this book then) The Copt is asked to talk about various Big Subjects. And yes, yes he does.<br />Elegance,Defeat, Love, and so forth.<br />The Copt has obviously read the basic texts of the folks he is chatting to, because his responses are dotted with bits from Isaiah and Matthew and mostly likely from the Koran (I'm not well versed in the Koran, so I didn't immediately recognize quotes as I did those from the Bible). And he does now and then sonorously contradict himself, but hey, it's all good.<br />And sure, there are good wise moments in this book. The same sort of good wise moments we meet again and again in our spiritual readings and recognize once again.<br />Like "Enthusiasm is Sacred Fire". Or "If we are happy we are on the right road"<br />It's a very slender book, so it will fit nicely in the pockets and backpacks of its admirers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3345848076570708125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6251001114149591308" style="display:none"><br>Preamble <br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/nqkXrQV" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417373i/825430.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/EfmvFgn" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a> <br><br>The Nag Hammadi manuscripts, The Dead Sea Scrolls and the Apocryphal Gospels have been for some years a source of a salutary religious and academic debate; even, from a fiction perspective, we could include Barbara Thiering thesis of a “married Jesus”, with kids…and much else….in these debates. <br><br><b>BUT</b>: somehow, Coelho managed to find another manuscript: Accra’s; and this one brings nothing of salutary, in my view. It’s not a novel. Supposedly, it’s a sort of discourses of a wise man to the people.<br><br> I’ve read “The Prophet” by Kahlil Gibran and found a lot of wisdom inside; not the same with Coelho’s, which seems to be a sort of collage of Gibran’s. <br><br><br> <b>Accra's story<br></b><br><br>On the 14th of July 1099, a Greek man, known as the Copt, summons people for a meeting in a plaza king Herod once used. <br><br>It’s crusades time; French troops are of superior power. The crowd is confronted with a dilemma: leave or fight to death?. They decided to stay... and listen to the wise man. <br><br>To Ibn Al-Athir it’s year 492; to Yacob it’s 4859; of course, Muslim and Jewish and Christian calendars are different. And yet, the Greek man believes in the Present moment….in the divine energy, in the Moira, the Unknown God. The multitude seeks him for answers; so they present questions: what’s knowledge?...what’s defeat?...and the defeated?...what’s solitude…etc. <br><br>The wise man delivers answers like: “nobody knows about what tomorrow will bring [the heck!...where have I heard/read this….already?]; as for “defeat”: “there’s neither defeat nor victory….only movement”; [I’m glad Hitler lost the war…and the Allies got victorious]. <br><br>Questions proceed,…but answers sometimes border the obvious; that’s why I interrupted the reading of this book. Someday,who knows,…I’ll get back to it. <br><br><br><b>By the way: the crowd should have left the place; it would have been wiser…in my view.</b></span>

<div id="review_572632359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/572632359" />
    <a title="Nancy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3122452-nancy"><img alt="Nancy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1292230382p2/3122452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/572632359?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/3122452-nancy">Nancy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer572632359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3903477015342923068">I really loved <i>The Alchemist</i> and Paulo Coelho shares deep wisdom within the story. This time the story is much more secondary as the different groups of people inside the walls of Jerusalem gather to hear the wisdom of a Greek man simply known as "The Copt." Tomorrow most will die so tonight they ask questions, make observations and listen to the Greek's wisdom. He speaks of love, life, death, regrets, family, friends, home, fear, faith and much, much more.<br/><br/>The book appeals to not only Christian,</span>
  <span id="freeText3903477015342923068" style="display:none">I really loved <i>The Alchemist</i> and Paulo Coelho shares deep wisdom within the story. This time the story is much more secondary as the different groups of people inside the walls of Jerusalem gather to hear the wisdom of a Greek man simply known as "The Copt." Tomorrow most will die so tonight they ask questions, make observations and listen to the Greek's wisdom. He speaks of love, life, death, regrets, family, friends, home, fear, faith and much, much more.<br /><br />The book appeals to not only Christian, but also Jewish and Muslim. The wisdom is basic truisms not always articulated and sometimes loaded with a great deal of insight. It is a book that is best read slowly and processed rather than something to be read between the activities of life.<br /><br />The book is based on a supposed manuscript found near Accra. Depending on the reader's spiritual and emotional travels through life, parts of the book will prove to reaffirm and provide insight. It is uplifting and builds greatly on hope and faith, along with the basic tenets of religion, organized or not. <br /><br />A book that every home library would benefit from having.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3903477015342923068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_594526027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/594526027" />
    <a title="Arthur" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6661400-arthur"><img alt="Arthur" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318600244p2/6661400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/594526027?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arthur" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arthur" href="/user/show/6661400-arthur">Arthur</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer594526027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7646475271733654020">The setting for this latest offering by Paulo Coelho is in Jerusalem. The date is July 14, 1099. On this date, the city was held by the Fatimids. Outside the city, the Crusaders are to make their final assault and enter the city. Most of the inhabitants of the city at this time profess one of the three Abrahamic religions: Judaism, Christianity, and Islam. Knowing that the Crusaders will soon attack, the people, vexed with uncertainty, are told to gather around a wise Greek simply known as the C</span>
  <span id="freeText7646475271733654020" style="display:none">The setting for this latest offering by Paulo Coelho is in Jerusalem. The date is July 14, 1099. On this date, the city was held by the Fatimids. Outside the city, the Crusaders are to make their final assault and enter the city. Most of the inhabitants of the city at this time profess one of the three Abrahamic religions: Judaism, Christianity, and Islam. Knowing that the Crusaders will soon attack, the people, vexed with uncertainty, are told to gather around a wise Greek simply known as the Copt. Some expected some sort of sermon; but instead the Copt wanted the people to ask questions that were troubling them. This dialogue would be set to writing or memorized for posterity. Certainly, many of them asked about what will happen the next day. But others asked some different questions about their life, love, dreams, disappointments, and fears. The book reminds me of "The Prophet" by Kahlil Gibran. I see this book as a continuation of his book "The Warrior of the Light". People who are expecting a novel when they pick this up, will be disappointed. But those who are willing to read through it, may benefit from some of the author's perspectives on some of life's most difficult problems.<br /><br />NB According to "Al-Kamil fi'l Tarikh" by the famous historian Ali ibn al-Athir, the Crusaders slaughtered 70,000 Muslims, including women and children, who took refuge in the Al-Aqsa Mosque.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7646475271733654020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2399086161579237207">Read by Jeremy Irons, Paulo Coelho's book, Manuscript Found in Accra (pronounced a CRA) is more than a book. It is a contemplation on human values that have endured the passage of time.<br/><br/>The story is told through the eyes of the Copt. It is 1099 in Jerusalem and the Crusaders are at the gate. The Copt has summoned the townspeople to address their fears. He talks of many things: defeat, struggle, the nature of the enemy; they contemplate the will to change and the virtues of loyalty and solitude; t</span>
  <span id="freeText2399086161579237207" style="display:none">Read by Jeremy Irons, Paulo Coelho's book, Manuscript Found in Accra (pronounced a CRA) is more than a book. It is a contemplation on human values that have endured the passage of time.<br /><br />The story is told through the eyes of the Copt. It is 1099 in Jerusalem and the Crusaders are at the gate. The Copt has summoned the townspeople to address their fears. He talks of many things: defeat, struggle, the nature of the enemy; they contemplate the will to change and the virtues of loyalty and solitude; they ultimately turn to questions about beauty, love, wisdom, sex, elegance and what the future holds.<br /><br />This is a book well worthy of a re-read (or in this case a listen followed by a read!!). On the second go-around, I will take each subject and provide one quote.<br /><br />To get us started, I will include one in this preliminary review.<br /><br />DEFEAT. Only he who gives up is defeated.<br /><br />4 stars</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer555513709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8567445059041217601">I felt like book was trying to be too much at once and as a result, it was not as successful as it could have been as a fictional STORY or a well-being/self-help book. <br/><br/>I began with the impression that this would be some historical fiction/history re-write and in some ways it is. I particularly enjoy how each chapter is an answer to a question - very parable-like, and it takes a narrative tone that the Bible has in many instances. However, there are no real characters that carry over chapter to c</span>
  <span id="freeText8567445059041217601" style="display:none">I felt like book was trying to be too much at once and as a result, it was not as successful as it could have been as a fictional STORY or a well-being/self-help book. <br /><br />I began with the impression that this would be some historical fiction/history re-write and in some ways it is. I particularly enjoy how each chapter is an answer to a question - very parable-like, and it takes a narrative tone that the Bible has in many instances. However, there are no real characters that carry over chapter to chapter, who we get know, and who develop in some way. It is just a narrator dispensing life advice and wisdom to a crowd. If I had known this book was going to be some Socratic/Jesus mash-up, I may have been less disappointed - but about as equally impressed (which is not much). <br /><br />As a work of non-fiction, well-being, or modern day pseudo-political philosophy book; it's rather disorganized, not very clear, and gratuitous with the examples (too many 'stories' that actually dilute the lesson rather than make it stronger). <br /><br />To me, this book is having an identity crisis. It has redeeming qualities: some genuinely thought provoking concepts and ideas - but none that haven't been discussed before in a more effective medium or narrative voice.<br /><br />1.5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="8567445059041217601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_571266286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/571266286" />
    <a title="Tia Bach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4197216-tia-bach"><img alt="Tia Bach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477083530p2/4197216.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/571266286?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tia Bach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tia Bach" href="/user/show/4197216-tia-bach">Tia Bach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer571266286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17564803986731059411">It's amazing to think how many manuscripts such as these were lost to us generations ago--that many scholars' thoughts and advice are lost to the ravages of time. <br/><br/>In 1099, the mysterious Copt is speaking to a crowd awaiting attack. In the face of death, the Copt shares his views on life. Some ask if they shouldn't instead be focused on preparing for battle, to which Copt replies, "Our task is not to leave a record of what happened on this date... history will take care of that. Therefore, we wil</span>
  <span id="freeText17564803986731059411" style="display:none">It's amazing to think how many manuscripts such as these were lost to us generations ago--that many scholars' thoughts and advice are lost to the ravages of time. <br /><br />In 1099, the mysterious Copt is speaking to a crowd awaiting attack. In the face of death, the Copt shares his views on life. Some ask if they shouldn't instead be focused on preparing for battle, to which Copt replies, "Our task is not to leave a record of what happened on this date... history will take care of that. Therefore, we will speak about our daily lives, about the difficulties we've had to face."<br /><br />He then answers a series of questions about everything from defeat, solitude, self-worth, and fear to beauty, our path in life, and love. <br /><br />So many of the Copt's answers spoke to me, and this book has been dog-eared, starred, highlighted, and shared. I know there will be days I will turn to it for strength and encouragement. Some highlights:<br /><br />Help us to understand that wisdom lies not in the answers we are given, but in the mystery of the questions that enrich our lives. p135<br /><br />Therefore, although anxiety is a part of life, never let it control you... If it tries to persuade you that taking on lots of jobs means having a productive life, say: "I need time to look at the stars in order to feel inspired and to be able to do my job well." p145<br /><br />Never miss an opportunity to show your love, especially to those close to you, because we are always at our most cautious with them for fear of being hurt... Love does not need to be understood. It needs only to be shown. p153 <br /><br />We all face times in our lives where the questions seem to outweigh the answers, a time where we are searching for wisdom. This book touches on so many of the topics that hold most of us back from becoming our best selves. It's a quick read, but it's packed with life-affirming and life-altering advice.<br /><br /><i>Note: I received a complimentary copy for review purposes. A positive review was not guaranteed or requested; the opinions expressed are my own.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17564803986731059411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_580577483" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/580577483" />
    <a title="Sally Walker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19072083-sally-walker"><img alt="Sally Walker" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/580577483?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sally Walker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sally Walker" href="/user/show/19072083-sally-walker">Sally Walker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer580577483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8780861111998457447">Pure wisdom<br/><br/>I have always loved Paulo Coelho’s books; they are so concise in a great way, so beautiful but challenging. He is simple but profound and his histories will make you rethink your whole world. Because all of that, I expected “Manuscript found in Accra” to be great. And it just… is. As other Coelho’s books, it takes you to another world and the story surrounds you in a beautiful way. You can’t stop reading and you see yourself immersed in a charming but deep history.<br/><br/>We live in a very ch</span>
  <span id="freeText8780861111998457447" style="display:none">Pure wisdom<br /><br />I have always loved Paulo Coelho’s books; they are so concise in a great way, so beautiful but challenging. He is simple but profound and his histories will make you rethink your whole world. Because all of that, I expected “Manuscript found in Accra” to be great. And it just… is. As other Coelho’s books, it takes you to another world and the story surrounds you in a beautiful way. You can’t stop reading and you see yourself immersed in a charming but deep history.<br /><br />We live in a very changing world, and “Manuscript found in Accra” just goes back to the beginning. I really appreciated that while I was reading, and I felt again that magic, like when I was 16 and I read “The Alchemist”. That magic is exactly what makes books great. And this new book makes you think about some of the most basic things of your life and your world. It is original but structured, easy to read and inspiring. As Paulo Coelho usually does, the new book is not very long, but it’s precise and intense, and it just gets to the point. Because it’s easy to read, I would recommend read it even twice! Some quotes and some sentences are so thoughtful that I would say that the whole book requires re-reading.<br /><br />Indeed, the plot, the quotes, the philosophy behind it… everything makes it just simple but at the same time magnificent. I couldn’t stop reading. It was just pure wisdom. Highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8780861111998457447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The words was full of wisdom, that's why i was really attracted into it. I got a copy of the book last two days ago.   <span id="freeText10991316296819078045" style="display:none">When I first found out about the book from my friend, when she posted a quotation from the book, i really got interested in reading it. The words was full of wisdom, that's why i was really attracted into it. I got a copy of the book last two days ago. And to my amazement, i only read it for just almost two hours! <br />This one is really a page turner. Every word and every detail brought so much knowledge and realizations over me. The main character which is the-so-called "Copt" serves as the source of a vast of wisdom, which is based merely on his experiences and personal search for meaning in this life. <br />While i was reading it, i felt like i was reading the book of Ecclesiastes in the Old Testament of the Bible. It has a vast view of the world we live in, and the experiences we come across in our daily life. The Copt is like a 'Preacher', who is very wise and has a deeper understanding of human nature. <br />Thumbs up to Paulo Coelho for making such wonderful books that inspires generations all over the world!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9190122927307353073">It's the first Coelho book I've read that might equal "The Alchemist" for message and enjoyment.<br/><br/>Honestly, though, it's like a modern language version of Gibran's "The Prophet". It's just got people on the eve of an assault asking questions of a religious man, instead of people asking a religious man questions on the eve of his departure to another land. <br/><br/>I want to own this book, read it slowly and write in the margins.<br/><br/>Do I think it's brilliant and amazing? No, because it's too much like "The Prop</span>
  <span id="freeText9190122927307353073" style="display:none">It's the first Coelho book I've read that might equal "The Alchemist" for message and enjoyment.<br /><br />Honestly, though, it's like a modern language version of Gibran's "The Prophet". It's just got people on the eve of an assault asking questions of a religious man, instead of people asking a religious man questions on the eve of his departure to another land. <br /><br />I want to own this book, read it slowly and write in the margins.<br /><br />Do I think it's brilliant and amazing? No, because it's too much like "The Prophet" to call is orignal.<br /><br />Do I think it has worthwhile insights and ideas to apply to living - oh, yes, most definitely yes.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer552209464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5594600309087571918">Those who are familiar with Coelho's work know that we must read between the lines to get the message. This book, however, answers the questions that we all make to ourselves at least once in our lives. I can guarantee that no matter how many times you read it, you will always get a different meaning from his answers. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1473649590" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1473649590" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1473649590?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007513925" href="/book/show/17470686-manuscript-found-in-accra">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=trees-died-for-this-crap">trees-died-for-this-crap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=1star">1star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2015">read2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1473649590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11636104479629061101">I had been looking for The Alchemist in my library but all I could locate was this Coelho book so I didn't know what to expect when I started to read it. The book sets itself out almost as if it's a factual book rather than a novel (is it supposed to be a fiction based on an actual manuscript???....it's not very clear...) The author tells us that the novel is a transcript of the words of wisdom that 'The Copt' gave to the members of a city, Jerusalem, the night before they were attacked. The Cop</span>
  <span id="freeText11636104479629061101" style="display:none">I had been looking for The Alchemist in my library but all I could locate was this Coelho book so I didn't know what to expect when I started to read it. The book sets itself out almost as if it's a factual book rather than a novel (is it supposed to be a fiction based on an actual manuscript???....it's not very clear...) The author tells us that the novel is a transcript of the words of wisdom that 'The Copt' gave to the members of a city, Jerusalem, the night before they were attacked. The Copt was said to be a learned man from Greece who did not follow any particular religion but was a believer in the unknown god referred to as Divine Energy. The book's chapters are not chapters as such, but are more like lectures given in answer to the spiritual questions of the people of Jerusalem to this Copt character. <br /><br />Eg. "What is true in love is also true in war. Losing a battle or losing everything we thought we possessed will bring us moments of sadness but when those moments pass we will discover the hidden strength that exists in each of us, a strength that will surprise us and increase our self respect. <br />We will look around and say to ourselves 'I survived'. And we will be cheered by our words. <br />Only those who fail to recognise that inner strength will say 'I lost' and be sad."<br /><br /><br />For the first forty pages or so this was all rather sweet and saccharine... And it had one or two thought provoking moments but it quickly grew tiresome. The novel just became more and more "preachy" in its tone and I grew more and more irritated by its overly simplistic view of life. The views of The Copt had no supporting evidence, there was no debate; the style of the novel was such that we were to accept this man's viewpoint as "gospel" (excuse the pun!). And indeed the viewpoints of The Copt were just a mash-up of various beliefs and philosophies from multiple existing religions; it all felt very unoriginal. <br /> <br />This was a very light and extremely quick read. It was probably well intentioned and there were some lovely passages in the book that would make for some lovely quotes. However, it all felt too much like a series of preachy, pretentious lectures one after another and it just wasn't my cup of tea. One star.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11636104479629061101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_578647862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/578647862" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19005855-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/578647862?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/19005855-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer578647862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6910493501564083638">Just perfect<br/><br/>Paulo Coelho is one of my favorite authors. He always writes such amazing books! And the best thing is that all his books are short, but at the same time intense and beautiful. I’ve always thought that he is simple but profound, and his histories make you rethink your whole world. I remember reading The Alchemist when I was 16… in a very specific way, it just changed me. And because of that, I wanted to read “Manuscript found in Accra” as soon as I got the chance. It is just… great. </span>
  <span id="freeText6910493501564083638" style="display:none">Just perfect<br /><br />Paulo Coelho is one of my favorite authors. He always writes such amazing books! And the best thing is that all his books are short, but at the same time intense and beautiful. I’ve always thought that he is simple but profound, and his histories make you rethink your whole world. I remember reading The Alchemist when I was 16… in a very specific way, it just changed me. And because of that, I wanted to read “Manuscript found in Accra” as soon as I got the chance. It is just… great. As other Coelho’s books, it takes you to another world and the story just surrounds you. You can’t stop reading and you see yourself immersed in a charming but deep history. “Manuscript found in Accra” just goes back to the beginning. I really appreciated that while I was reading, and I felt again that magic, like when I read “The Alchemist”. That magic is exactly what makes books great. And this new book makes you think about some of the most basic things of your life and your world. It is original but structured, easy to read and inspiring. Just perfect… as always.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6910493501564083638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OydQplQfGhD7eWcIa0nOffyIDki5dk5Lsap6+3QiDSyszkk/aEIcOQDiKSw4nPZTn+tdCYGYe7t/AtjHjZXSiQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

He was known as the &quot;boy who was born dead&quot; and who ultimately survived against all odds. Before he became internationally known as a worldwide bestselling author, Paulo lived many different lives. He flirted with suicide, was committed by his parents to insane asylums, suffered the brutality of electric shock therapy, dove into drugs, tried several varieties of sex, met the devil, spent time in prison, helped revolutionize Brazilian rock with musician Raul Seixas, and finally rediscovered his faith in 1986 as he walked the sacred Road to Santiago de Compostela, a medieval pilgrim\'s route between France and Spain.\n\nCoelho would later describe this life-changing spiritual experience in his first book, The Pilgrimage. The following year, The Alchemist established his worldwide reputation. The novel has already achieved the status of a universally admired modern classic.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho">About Paulo Coelho</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/566.Paulo_Coelho"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1201840056p3/566.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7663385130380111250">The Brazilian author PAULO COELHO was born in 1947 in the city of Rio de Janeiro. Before dedicating his life completely to literature, he worked as theatre director and actor, lyricist and journalist. In 1986, PAULO COELHO did the pilgrimage to Saint James of Compostella, an experience later to be documented in his book The Pilgrimage. In the following year, COELHO published The Alchemist. Slow in</span>
  <span id="freeText7663385130380111250" style="display:none">The Brazilian author PAULO COELHO was born in 1947 in the city of Rio de Janeiro. Before dedicating his life completely to literature, he worked as theatre director and actor, lyricist and journalist. In 1986, PAULO COELHO did the pilgrimage to Saint James of Compostella, an experience later to be documented in his book The Pilgrimage. In the following year, COELHO published The Alchemist. Slow initial sales convinced his first publisher to drop the novel, but it went on to become one of the best selling Brazilian books of all time. Other titles include Brida (1990), The Valkyries (1992), By the river Piedra I sat Down and Wept (1994), the collection of his best columns published in the Brazilian newspaper Folha de São Paulo entitle Maktub (1994), the compilation of texts Phrases (1995), The Fifth Mountain (1996), Manual of a Warrior of Light (1997), Veronika decides to die (1998), The Devil and Miss Prym (2000), the compilation of traditional tales in Stories for parents, children and grandchildren (2001), Eleven Minutes (2003), The Zahir (2005), The Witch of Portobello (2006) and Winner Stands Alone (to be released in 2009). During the months of March, April, May and June 2006, Paulo Coelho traveled to celebrate the 20th anniversary of his pilgrimage to Saint James of Compostella in 1986. He also held surprise book signings - announced one day in advance - in some cities along the way, to have a chance to meet his readers. In ninety days of pilgrimage the author traveled around the globe and took the famous Transiberrian train that took him to Vladivostok. During this experience Paulo Coelho launched his blog Walking the Path - The Pilgrimage in order to share with his readers his impressions. Since this first blog Paulo Coelho has expanded his presence in the internet with his daily blogs in Wordpress, Myspace &amp; Facebook. He is equally present in media sharing sites such as Youtube and Flickr, offering on a regular basis not only texts but also videos and pictures to his readers. From this intensive interest and use of the Internet sprang his bold new project: The Experimental Witch where he invites his readers to adapt to the screen his book The Witch of Portobello. Indeed Paulo Coelho is a firm believer of Internet as a new media and is the first Best-selling author to actively support online free distribution of his work. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7663385130380111250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
